# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Rust Macro Expansion to HIR Lowering Chain

## Your Task

Trace how Rust procedural macros and declarative macros are expanded and lowered to HIR in rust-lang/rust. Find Rust source files implementing: the macro expander entry point, the token stream transformation, the AST expansion, and the HIR lowering from expanded AST.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7, sg-evals/servo--be6a2f99.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7` (rust-lang/rust)
- `sg-evals/servo--be6a2f99` (servo/servo)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json

```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

A \"matcher position\" (a.k.a. \"position\" or \"mp\") is a dot in the middle of a matcher, usually\n18: //! written as a `·`. ## Key Files Identified

**Macro Expansion Core:**
- `compiler/rustc_expand/src/expand.rs` - Main `MacroExpander` with expansion logic
- `compiler/rustc_expand/src/base.rs` - Extension context and trait definitions

**Declarative Macros (macro_rules!):**
- `compiler/rustc_expand/src/mbe/macro_rules.rs` - Macro-by-example expansion
- `compiler/rustc_expand/src/mbe/macro_parser.rs` - NFA-based pattern matching
- `compiler/rustc_expand/src/mbe/transcribe.rs` - Token stream transformation

**Procedural Macros:**
- `compiler/rustc_expand/src/proc_macro.rs` - Bang and attribute macro handling
- `compiler/rustc_expand/src/proc_macro_server.rs` - Proc macro bridge server

**HIR Lowering:**
- `compiler/rustc_ast_lowering/src/lib.rs` - Main HIR lowering entry point
- `compiler/rustc_ast_lowering/src/item.rs` - Item lowering

**Integration:**
- `compiler/rustc_interface/src/passes.rs` - Orchestrates the expansion and lowering pipeline

## Expansion Chain

1. **expand_crate** → Initiates macro expansion
2. **fully_expand_fragment** → Recursively expands all macros
3. **collect_invocations** → Finds macro invocations and creates placeholders
4. **expand_invoc** → Dispatches to specific macro implementations
5. **TtParser** (for declarative macros) → Matches macro patterns
6. **transcribe** → Transforms matched tokens
7. **parse_ast_fragment** → Converts expanded tokens back to AST
8. **lower_to_hir** → Converts expanded AST to HIR

There's a set of current NFA threads\\n3: //! and a set of next ones. Instead of NTs, we have a special case for Kleene star. The big-O, in\\n4: //! pathological cases, is worse than traditional use of NFA or Earley parsing, but it's an easier\\n5: //! fit for Macro-by-Example-style rules.\\n6: //!\\n7: //! (In order to prevent the pathological case, we'd need to lazily construct the resulting\\n8: //! `NamedMatch`es at the very end. We don't say this parser uses the Earley algorithm, because it's unnecessarily inaccurate.\\n12: //! The macro parser restricts itself to the features of finite state automata. Earley parsers\\n13: //! can be described as an extension of NFAs with completion rules, prediction rules, and recursion.\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Quick intro to how the parser works:\\n16: //!\\n17: //!
